<rating>5</rating>< review>
My two toddler sons and I enjoyed a nice day at Davies park today. This was our first visit to the park and we will for sure be back soon. My 3 year old loved the excavator digging toys. There is LOTS of sand in the play area so be prepared for that. The park has two very nice basketball courts, tennis courts, a large field for soccer, bathrooms, and large rocks to climb and explore.< /review>

< Text>
This Park is great for all Ages and family. Tennis courts, Basketball Courts, Jungle Gym in the Sandbox area, and a huge Soccer Field! Also lots of Big Boulders Surrounding the park to Explore. Many Covered Areas to throw parties and Events. Highly Recommended for everyone! This place is FANTASTIC & very SAFE! Extremely Clean and well Lit. Parking lots are small but theres street parking as well.</Text>

<UserId.>108910586828582139473< /UserId.><name>Keely Dorran< /name><time>1418802973123<//time>< rating>
5< /rating>
< text>
I was born in 1972 and lived in a small house on my grandparents' property here with my parents and sister for several years. My mom had a horse ranch, they had some cattle, and her father was a medical Dr. who had a practice in Folsom until he passed on in the mid-1970s. My grandmother sold the property eventually and I was sad about that until I discovered that the developers/county saved the huge granite boulders we played on as kids and built this park around them! And The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints built a meeting house right were our old driveway and part of the house were. I bring my own child here to play since he was born in '98- what a delight! And we enjoy family picnics here now. There are indian grinding stones in some of the granite boulders from when the Maidu lived here, before the Gold Rush in 1849.</text>

<Rate>3<//Rate><text>We had dinner at Noah's for first time with friends.
The waitstaff was very attentive. However,the following are my observations regarding the full experience.
AMBIENCE: the bar has at least one tv. Also there's a "lounge" in the same room. That makes it a sport bar/lounge (???).
We sat at the back room, which was bright, very bright which suggests it's also a family style restaurant.
WINE LIST: pretty good selection, including local wines. Reasonable prices.
The server came to the table holding glasses like they're full and asked who's trying it first.  When the ok was given he filled glass of taster first.
FOOD:Started with a salad to start. The salad came first and was big enough to share between four of us.
Then ordered Chicken Parmesan, Artichoke Pasta, New York steak and Rib-eye steak for diner. Minutes later they notified us no Rib-eye was available. No problem, we ordered something else.
The Artichoke pasta was ok, as well as the chicken Parmesan which suggested us it was chicken cutlet, but was half chicken with bones and melted cheese on top. Also was "almost ok".
The New York steak was ordered medium rare and was cooked to perfection.
The salad ordered first was perfect for the steak, so we're enjoying it like that, but a waitress came and asked us if we want a container for the salad... which we were still eating... then, 5 minutes later comes again and asked us if we wanted another glass of wine, not noticing we had a bottle at our table...

OVERALL: A restaurant with multiple identities, Sports bar/ lounge/family style restaurant, with a nice wine menu, a dinner menu that could be improved (both in BOH and in the menu itself,  an attentive staff that could make the experience even better if trained for it.

I'm pretty sure I'm missing something in my notes. I really wanted to give our waiter a few tips from my long experience in the industry but don't wanted to make him feel I was putting him in the spot.

I wish you the best and I might visit you when back to the west coast.<//text><Date>1488272748019<//Date><resp>None</resp>< user>

< Text>
This is where our local discount store, The Dollar Tree is located. The store is usually packed and the lines are long, but it is a good spot to get basic home necessities. There is a community center next door to the store for local community, where the Boys and Girls Club and a resource library is housed, all for low income and that is really needed here. There is plenty of parking. Lock your car for sure though. There are several questionable folks who hang around outside to the side of the building.<//Text>

<time>1546816104702< /time>< gmapID>
0x808437f986655fc7:0x660f9b6c817c56c7</gmapID>
< Review>
Politics! This was in County. For years there was debate about annexation by the City. It's in the traditional low income, neglected Southwest quadrant of town. There was an Albertsons Market anchor, operating profitably until Lucky merger, then it closed, remained vacant. Next, the bowling alley closed, remained vacant, creating more urban blight. City would not annex unless County had Redevelopment in place. Then, Redevelopment collapsed. The annexation of a large area known as Roseland, a bustling community, was completed in 2018. It is a work in progress! Plans for a Community Village, shops, and housing exist.
Now 3/4 vacant, buildings demolished, it's home to Dollar Tree, several thriving Hispanic markets, my favorite Taqueria, and the first branch of the Library in the S/W. New homes, improved streets, City water, sewage, new Parks are all around it. A historical perspective is essential to any critical review. Stay tuned for further development.< /Review>

<user_id>108709054647716081162<//user_id><Pictures>None< /Pictures>< review>
This is complicated by politics/economics. It is not now a "shopping center", it is a yet to be fulfilled promise to residents of the S/W "Roseland" area by City/County officials. Formerly anchored by an Albertsons market and a bowling alley (both now demolished) it is now largely vacant. Roseland has evolved in the last 30+ years to have the highest density Hispanic population in Santa Rosa. Previously, it was low income whites, who resisted for years local government efforts to incorporate it into the city.
There have been law enforcement conflicts over jurisdiction of the area. The Sheriff at one point told the Chief of Police to have his personnel "stand down", their manner of policing in an area of no jurisdiction was creating, not resolving, police problems. The City told County they did not want to annex unless County (Sonoma) had a redevelopment. plan in place. Back and forth. Who's paying for conforming to City standards (sewer, water, sidewalks, etc.) ? The library has opened a branch and become a gathering place to discuss plans.
Otherwise, it's a large parking lot where groups meet (car clubs, native dancers). Not a plaza, nor Mercado yet. A work in progress.< /review>

<rating>3< /rating>< review>
Best vape shop in Atwater which isn't saying much. They have a decent selection and most things are in stock most of the time but they are popular so it makes sense that they'd run out of something but usually they'll have it in the next day or so. As for the prices, well, it's typical of vape shops to be way over priced compared to online and this one is no different. The main dude that works most of the time is cool but his little helper is an angry little man with an attitude who has absolutely zero knowledge about any of the products they sell. If you don't believe me just go in there and ask him a question about anything that you already know the answer to and you will either ask the main guy who usually knows or he'll give you some bogus response half the time. For example if you're looking for a coil for your atomizer (it better be smok or compatible with baby beast or prince cuz that's all they have) he seems to think they are all universally compatible. If you don't need whatever you're trying to buy immediately it's best to just shop online and save your money.< /review>

If you‚Äôre looking for a unique historic place you‚Äôre in for a treat. Established back in 1850s  you‚Äôll see so much history as you walk in. < text>
Giving it 5 stars for what it is, a true country bar with rural food. It's not a place for foodies, it's a place to get a cold beer at a very old bar, and the grub is good.

The location has a bit of history as well dating back to the civil war, see the monument out front.

My go-to is the chicken or the burger. I believe they teamed up with a local artisen dairy operation a couple of years ago. That said, the cheese and ice cream are both fantastic, meaning what you'd expect at a 5 star in SF.</text>

< user>
116021218278140924238< /user>
< review>
I came here with a friend at around 8PM on a Friday. The service was on point, and the Prime Rib was cooked to perfection.

The location of Washoe House lends itself to a pretty diverse blend of visitors. You'll absolutely see people fresh off of the farm or ranch coming in to have dinner, you'll see tourists walking through the front door staring at the ceiling, and you'll see other folks walk in and talk to the staff like they are old friends (they probably are!)

The food was fantastic. Even though it was busy, we received prompt and courteous service throughout the dinner. The drinks came out shortly after being ordered, and our server took the time to explain the menu, go over the specials, and tell us her recommendations. Friday Night they have a prime rib special. I am so happy I ordered it! It was late in the dinner window, but the prime rib I got was fantastic. Before the entree, they brought biscuits and a local cheese plate out to try. I thought that was a nice touch.

The service was great. Not only was it great, it has a "small town feel." Within a few minutes of walking in, you'll probably be having a conversation with someone about something. It's a place where a guy (or gal) off the ranch will have a conversation with someone in a suit about hunting.

You can see a division in reviews - with the "old" owners, and with the "new" owners. It is clear that the new management is doing what they can to restore this historic stop as a place to go for good food, good drinks, and good people. I think they are executing this well.<//review>

< Review>
Been going here for a long time. Cool old roadhouse that is a historical landmark and an iconic destination in Sonoma County.
The place has had several changes in ownership over the years and has remained mostly consistent.
The food is good most of the time depending on your server and how busy it is.
We recently went on a Friday night and it was crazy busy so our experience wasn't that good. The kicker for me was a watered down cocktail that tasted like dishwater. I returned it and was still charged for it when the bill came. Food was good but had to ask for bread twice during dinner.
If it's not crazy busy then I would give it 4 stars for atmosphere and good food.
Great for a burger and beer on the way home from the county dump. Been doing that for years.
Ok, so I added another star and am updating my review because the last few times I have been here for lunch it has been outstanding both in service and food quality. I just had the French Dip for lunch and it was succulent and habit forming. They now also serve breakfast and although I haven't tried it yet I'll bet it's good.
Everybody has a bad service experience once in awhile. All is forgivin!</Review>
